TITLE      Scattering of 19-30-MeV Alpha Particles from C12       C208300100003 
AUTHOR     (J.F.Morgan,R.K.Hobbie)                                C208300100004 
REFERENCE  (J,PR/C,1,(1),155,1970)                                C208300100005 
           #doi:10.1103/PhysRevC.1.155                            C208300100006 
INSTITUTE  (1USAMIN)                                              C208300100007 
FACILITY   (VDGT,1USAMIN)                                         C208300100008 
PART-DET   (A)                                                    C208300100009 
DETECTOR   (SIBAR)                                                C208300100010 
METHOD     For the excitation functions, eight ORTEC              C208300100011 
           surface barrier detectors were mounted on a            C208300100012 
           35-cm-diam. ring which fit into the scattering         C208300100013 
           chamber. This allowed each angle to be set             C208300100014 
           independently to +-0.1 degree. Solid angles for the    C208300100015 
           rectangular apertures, determined by measurement       C208300100016 
           with a traveling microscope to 1% accuracy, were       C208300100017 
           typically 0.500 msr; the angular acceptance was 0.5    C208300100018 
           degree. For most of the differential cross-section     C208300100019 
           measurements, three surface-barrier detectors were     C208300100020 
           used, mounted 30 degrees apart. Circular apertures     C208300100021 
           gave an angular acceptance of 1.2' and a typical       C208300100022 
           solid angle of 3.50 +- 0.04 msr. The electronic        C208300100023 
           equipment was conventional. Since only 4 ABC's were    C208300100024 
           available, more than four detectors were accommodated  C208300100025 
           by routing the ABC output. All of the digitized        C208300100026 
           signals were fed a CDC 3100 computer, in which a       C208300100027 
           block of memory was assigned to each detector.         C208300100028 
ERR-ANALYS No uncertainties are given in curves. The  statistical C208300100029 
           accuracy of the final data varied due to  the rapid    C208300100030 
           fluctuation of yield with energy and angle;  a cross   C208300100031 
           section of 10 mb was measured to a  statistical        C208300100032 
           accuracy of approximately 3%. The  accuracy of the     C208300100033 
           beam charge measurement was better  than 2%.           C208300100034
